## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch/reactor ODE rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard modeling object in chemical kinetics and reactor engineering. With only (t, A) available, the most common relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, equilibrium relaxation) and possibly explicit time-dependence (changing conditions, catalyst decay, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, dilute-limit kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction when other reactant is proportional to A)
- Nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fit)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-acceleration with finite capacity or product inhibition lumped into c1)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible/limited-rate (rational) law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective saturation/availability limitation without introducing extra species)
- Time-dependent first-order (catalyst deactivation/conditioning): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate constant decays over time)
- Aging/activation ramp: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate turns on as system equilibrates/mixes/heats)
- Diffusion/mass-transfer-limited transient: dA_dt = -c0 * A / sqrt(t + c1) (boundary-layer growth giving ~t^{-1/2} decay of transfer coefficient)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., feed/light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (consumption with oscillatory source term)
- Mixed polynomial kinetics (lumped mechanisms): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (superposition of background source/sink plus linear/quadratic pathways)
- Coupled time-and-concentration power law: dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A**c3 (empirical drift in effective rate constant over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Monotone depletion of a reactant A is often captured by enforcing dA_dt <= 0 for A > 0 (structures like -c0*A**n or -c0*(A-c1)).
- Observation of an asymptote A(t) -> c1 suggests equilibrium/steady-state relaxation forms dA_dt = -c0*(A-c1) rather than pure decay to zero.
- Strong early-time curvature that weakens with time can indicate transport limitation, motivating factors like 1/sqrt(t+c1) multiplying A.
- Sigmoidal A(t) (slow-fast-slow) is a hallmark of autocatalysis or self-limiting growth/decay, suggesting dA_dt proportional to A*(c1-A).
- If the apparent rate constant decreases over time independent of A, include explicit time modulation such as exp(-c*t) multiplying an A-dependent rate.
- If dA_dt magnitude grows less than proportionally with A at high concentration, rational forms like A/(1+c*A) mimic effective saturation/availability limits.
- Oscillations or repeated accelerations in dA_dt vs t at comparable A indicate external forcing; add sinusoidal (or other periodic) time terms.
- If data show sign changes in dA_dt at a fixed A (net production vs consumption), include additive source terms (c0 or time-forcing) rather than purely multiplicative decay.
- Mechanism switching (e.g., induction period then reaction) is often represented by time-gated terms (functions of t that transition between regimes) multiplying a base rate law.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK31)

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A + c2*_w*cos(log(A + c3))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.5980*sqrt(A) - 0.5980*A + 0.3066*cos(log(A + 1))`

This has three basis functions: `sqrt(A)`, `A`, and `cos(log(A+1))`.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The key question is whether any candidate can produce the `cos(log(A+1))` term, since that's the most distinctive part of the GT.

**Key observations:**
- The GT has no dependence on `t`, so any candidate with `t` terms must have those coefficients set to 0.
- The GT requires `cos(log(A+1))` which is an oscillatory function of `log(A+1)`.
- Polynomials, power laws (`A^c`), `1/A^(1/n)`, `exp(...)`, simple `log(...)`, and rational functions CANNOT produce `cos(log(A+1))`.

Let me check candidates that might produce oscillatory behavior:

**Candidate 15:** `A^c0*c1 + c2 + c3/(A+c4) + c5*exp(c6*|c7*log(A*c8+1)|)`
The exp of |log| term cannot produce cos(log(A+1)). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 28:** `A*c0/sqrt(c1+t) + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + A^c5*c6/A^(1/5) + c7/A^(1/5)`
Setting t-dependent terms to 0: `c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + A^(c5-1/5)*c6 + c7/A^(1/5)`. The sin term is `sin(A*c3+c4)`, not `cos(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 34:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c5/(A*c6+1) + c7*exp(A*c8)`
Setting t-terms: sin becomes sin(c4) which is constant. Cannot produce cos(log(A+1)). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 40:** `A*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + c4 + c5/A^(1/4) + c6/A^(1/5)`
sin(A*c2+c3) ≠ cos(log(A+1)). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 49:** Has `(|A|+1)^c4` which for A≥0 is `(A+1)^c4`. With complex c4, this could theoretically produce cos(log(A+1)) since `(A+1)^{iy} = e^{iy*log(A+1)} = cos(y*log(A+1)) + i*sin(y*log(A+1))`. But we need real constants, and real powers of (A+1) cannot produce cosine. [NO MATCH]

For all remaining candidates (1-14, 16-27, 29-33, 35-48, 50): None contain any mechanism to produce `cos(log(A+1))`. They consist of polynomials, power laws, exponentials, logarithms, and rational functions - none of which can combine to form `cos(log(A+1))`.

Going through each:
- Candidates with only polynomial/power/rational/exp/log terms: ALL [NO MATCH] because `cos(log(A+1))` cannot be represented by these basis functions.

Let me verify there's no candidate I missed with cosine or complex exponential capability... No, none of the candidates have the ability to produce `cos(log(A+1))`.
